<p>The <b>2006 FIFA World Cup</b> was the 18th <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decennial" title="Decennial">quadrennial</a> international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> world championship tournament. It was held from 9 June to 9 July 2006 in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, which won the right to <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_hosts#2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup hosts">host</a> the event in July 2000. <a href="/wiki/List_of_men%27s_national_association_football_teams" title="List of men's national association football teams">Teams</a> representing 198 national football associations from all six populated continents participated in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification">qualification</a> process which began in September 2003. Thirty-one teams qualified from this process, along with the host nation, <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>, for the finals tournament. It was the second time that Germany staged the competition (the first was in 1974 as West Germany and also a re-FIFA World Cup), and the tenth time that it was held in Europe.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> won the tournament, claiming their fourth World Cup title. They defeated <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> 5–3 in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(football)" title="Penalty shootout (football)">penalty shootout</a> in the final, after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time" title="Extra time">extra time</a> had finished in a 1–1 draw. Germany defeated <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> 3–1 to finish in third place. Angola, Ghana, Ivory Coast, Serbia and Montenegro, Trinidad and Tobago, and Togo made their first appearances in the finals.</p>
<p>The 2006 World Cup stands as one of the most watched events in television history, garnering an estimated 26.29 billion non-unique viewers, compiled over the course of the tournament. The final attracted an estimated audience of 715.1 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The 2006 World Cup ranks fourth in non-unique viewers, behind the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">World Cup in 1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> As the winner, Italy represented the World in the <a href="/wiki/2009_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2009 FIFA Confederations Cup">2009 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_selection">Host selection</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_hosts" title="FIFA World Cup hosts">FIFA World Cup hosts</a></div>
<p>The vote to choose the hosts of the 2006 tournament was held in July 2000 in <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, Switzerland. It involved four bidding nations after <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> had withdrawn three days earlier: <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Three rounds of voting were required, each round eliminating the nation with the least votes. The first two rounds were held on 6 July 2000, and the final round was held on 7 July 2000, which Germany won over South Africa.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bribery_and_corruption_allegations">Bribery and corruption allegations</span></h3>
<p>Accusations of bribery and corruption have marred the success of Germany's bid from the very beginning. On the very day of the vote, a hoax bribery affair was made public, leading to calls for a re-vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> On the night before the vote, German satirical magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(magazine)" title="Titanic (magazine)">Titanic</a></i> sent letters to FIFA representatives, offering joke gifts like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuckoo_clocks" title="Cuckoo clocks">cuckoo clocks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest_ham" title="Black Forest ham">Black Forest ham</a> in exchange for their vote for Germany. Oceania delegate <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Dempsey" title="Charlie Dempsey">Charlie Dempsey</a>, who had initially backed England, had then been instructed to support South Africa following England's elimination. He abstained, citing "intolerable pressure" on the eve of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Had Dempsey voted as originally instructed, the vote would have resulted with a 12–12 tie, and FIFA president <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Blatter" title="Sepp Blatter">Sepp Blatter</a>, who favoured the South African bid,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> would have had to cast the deciding vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>More irregularities surfaced soon after, including, in the months leading up to the decision, the sudden interest of German politicians and major businesses in the four Asian countries whose delegates were decisive for the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sueddeutsche_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-sueddeutsche-9">[9]</a></sup> Just a week before the vote, the German government under <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Schr%C3%B6der" title="Gerhard Schröder">Gerhard Schröder</a> lifted their arms embargo on <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and agreed to send grenade launchers to the country. <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">DaimlerChrysler</a> invested several hundred million Euro in <a href="/wiki/Hyundai" title="Hyundai">Hyundai</a>, while one of the sons of the company's founders was a member of FIFA's executive committee. Both <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayer" title="Bayer">Bayer</a> announced investments in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, whose respective delegates <a href="/wiki/Worawi_Makudi" title="Worawi Makudi">Worawi Makudi</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chung_Jong-Moon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chung Jong-Moon (page does not exist)">Chung Jong-Moon</a> were possible votes for Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sueddeutsche_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-sueddeutsche-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zeit_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-zeit-10">[10]</a></sup> Makudi additionally received a payment by a company of German media mogul <a href="/wiki/Leo_Kirch" title="Leo Kirch">Leo Kirch</a>, who also paid millions for usually worthless TV rights for friendly matches of the <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">German team</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sueddeutsche_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-sueddeutsche-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zeit_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-zeit-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 October 2015, the German news magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> alleged that a slush fund with money from then-<a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis-Dreyfus" title="Robert Louis-Dreyfus">Robert Louis-Dreyfus</a> was used to influence the vote of four Asian members of the FIFA executive committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The sum of 6.7 million Euro was later demanded back by Dreyfus. In order to retrieve the money, the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Organizing_Committee" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Organizing Committee">Organizing Committee</a> paid an aquivalent sum to the FIFA, allegedly as a German share for the cost of a closing ceremony, which never materialized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sueddeutsche_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-sueddeutsche-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Niersbach" title="Wolfgang Niersbach">Wolfgang Niersbach</a>, president of the <a href="/wiki/German_Football_Association" title="German Football Association">German Football Association</a> (DFB), denied the allegations on 17 October 2015, saying that "the World Cup was not bought" and that he could "absolutely and categorically rule out the existence of a slush fund". The DFB announced they would consider seeking legal action against Der Spiegel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> During a press conference on 22 October 2015, Nierbach repeated his stance, emphasizing that the 6,7 million were used in 2002 to secure a subsidy by FIFA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> According to Niersbach, the payment had been agreed upon during a meeting between <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a> and FIFA president Blatter, with the money being provided by Dreyfus. On the same day, FIFA contradicted Niersbach's statement, saying: "By our current state of knowledge, no such payment of 10 million Franks was registered by FIFA in 2002."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The following day, former DFB president <a href="/wiki/Theo_Zwanziger" title="Theo Zwanziger">Theo Zwanziger</a> publicly accused Niersbach of lying, saying: "It is evident that there was a slush fund for the German World Cup application". According to Zwanziger, the 6.7 million Euros went to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohamed_Bin_Hammam" title="Mohamed Bin Hammam">Mohamed Bin Hammam</a>, who at the time was supporting Blatter's campaign for president against <a href="/wiki/Issa_Hayatou" title="Issa Hayatou">Issa Hayatou</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 March 2016 it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ethics_Committee" title="FIFA Ethics Committee">FIFA Ethics Committee</a> was opening proceedings into the bid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification">Qualification</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification">2006 FIFA World Cup qualification</a></div>
<p>198 teams attempted to qualify for the 2006 World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Germany, the host nation, was granted automatic qualification, with the remaining 31 finals places divided among the continental confederations. Thirteen places were contested by <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> teams (Europe), five by <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">CAF</a> teams (Africa), four by <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a> teams (South America), four by <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">AFC</a> teams (Asia), and three by <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> teams (North and Central America and Caribbean). The remaining two places were decided by playoffs between AFC and CONCACAF and between CONMEBOL and <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">OFC</a> (Oceania).</p>
<p>Eight nations qualified for the finals for the first time: <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_football_team" title="Angola national football team">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team" title="Czech Republic national football team">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_football_team" title="Ivory Coast national football team">Ivory Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Togo_national_football_team" title="Togo national football team">Togo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Serbia and Montenegro national football team">Serbia and Montenegro</a>. Czech Republic and Ukraine were making their first appearance as independent nations, but had previously been represented as part of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> respectively; Serbia and Montenegro had competed as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> in 1998, as well as making up part of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslav</a> teams from 1930 to 1990. As of 2014, this was the last time <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_national_football_team" title="Saudi Arabia national football team">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>, Togo, Angola, Czech Republic, <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a>, Ukraine and Trinidad and Tobago qualified for a FIFA World Cup finals.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a> qualified for the first time since 1974. Among the teams who failed to qualify were 2002 third-placed team <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2004" title="Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a>. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> failed to qualify for the first time since 1978, and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> failed to qualify for the first time since 1986. <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> had their first successful qualifying campaign since 1986, as they did not qualify for the 1990 and 1994 World Cups, in 1998 they were automatically qualified as hosts and in 2002 as defending champions.</p>
<p>For the first time since the 1982 World Cup, all six confederations were represented at the finals tournament.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span></h2>
<p>In 2006, Germany had a plethora of football stadia that satisfied <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>'s minimum capacity of 40,000 seats for World Cup matches. The still-standing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Munich)" title="Olympic Stadium (Munich)">Olympiastadion</a> in Munich (69,250) was not used even though FIFA's regulations allow one city to use two stadia; <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LTU_Arena" title="LTU Arena">LTU Arena</a> (51,500), <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weserstadion" title="Weserstadion">Weserstadion</a> (43,000) and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Mönchengladbach">Mönchengladbach</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Borussia-Park" title="Borussia-Park">Borussia-Park</a> (46,249) were also unemployed during the tournament.</p>
<p>Twelve stadia were selected to host the World Cup matches. During the tournament, many of them were known by different names, as FIFA prohibits <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">sponsorship</a> of stadia unless the stadium sponsors were also official FIFA sponsors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StadiaNames_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-StadiaNames-21">[21]</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a> in Munich was known during the competition as <i>FIFA World Cup Stadium, Munich</i> (or in German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>FIFA WM-Stadion München</i></span>), and even the letters of the company <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a> were removed or covered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StadiaNames_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-StadiaNames-21">[21]</a></sup> Some of the stadia also had a lower capacity for the World Cup, as FIFA regulations ban standing room; nonetheless, this was accommodated as several stadia had an <a href="/wiki/UEFA_stadium_categories" title="UEFA stadium categories">UEFA 5-star ranking</a>.</p>
<center>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Squads">Squads</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_squads" title="2006 FIFA World Cup squads">2006 FIFA World Cup squads</a>.</div>
<p>Squads for the 2006 World Cup consisted of 23 players, as in the previous tournament in <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup_squads" title="2002 FIFA World Cup squads">2002</a>. Each participating national association had to confirm its 23-player <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_squads" title="2006 FIFA World Cup squads">squad</a> by 15 May 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Groups">Groups</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seeds">Seeds</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_seeding" title="2006 FIFA World Cup seeding">2006 FIFA World Cup seeding</a></div>
<p>The eight <a href="/wiki/Seed_(sports)" title="Seed (sports)">seeded</a> teams for the 2006 tournament were announced on 6 December 2005. The seeds comprised Pot A in the draw. Pot B contained the unseeded qualifiers from South America, Africa and Oceania; Pot C contained eight of the nine remaining European teams, excluding <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Serbia and Montenegro national football team">Serbia and Montenegro</a>. Pot D contained unseeded teams from the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> region and Asia. A special pot contained Serbia and Montenegro: this was done to ensure that no group contained three European teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In the special pot, Serbia and Montenegro was drawn first, then their group was drawn from the three seeded non-European nations, <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a>.</p>
<p>It had been predetermined that, as the host, <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> would be placed in Group A, thus being assured of the venues of their group matches in advance of the draw. FIFA had also announced in advance that Brazil (the defending champion) would be allocated to Group F.</p>

</table>
<p>On 9 December 2005 the draw was held, and the group assignments and order of matches were determined. After the draw was completed, commentators remarked that Group C appeared to be the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_death" title="Group of death">group of death</a>, while others suggested Group E.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Argentina and the Netherlands both qualified with a game to spare with wins over Ivory Coast and Serbia and Montenegro respectively.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_system">Group system</span></h3>
<p>The first round, or group stage, saw the thirty-two teams divided into eight groups of four teams. Each group was a <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round-robin</a> of three games, where each team played one match against each of the other teams in the same group. Teams were awarded three points for a win, one point for a draw and none for a defeat. The teams coming first and second in each group qualified for the Round of 16.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ranking_criteria">Ranking criteria</span></h4>
<p>If teams were level on points, they were ranked on the following criteria in order:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<ol>
<li>Greatest total goal difference in the three group matches</li>
<li>Greatest number of goals scored in the three group matches</li>
<li>If teams remained level after those criteria, a mini-group would be formed from those teams, who would be ranked on:
<ol>
<li>Most points earned in matches against other teams in the tie</li>
<li>Greatest goal difference in matches against other teams in the tie</li>
<li>Greatest number of goals scored in matches against other teams in the tie</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>If teams remained level after all these criteria, FIFA would hold a drawing of lots</li>
</ol>
</blockquote>
<p>In the original version of the rules for the final tournament, the ranking criteria were in a different order, with head-to-head results taking precedence over total goal difference. The rules were changed to the above in advance of the tournament, but older versions were still available on the FIFA and UEFA websites, causing some confusion among those trying to identify the correct criteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In any event, the final tournament saw only two pairs of teams level on points: Argentina and the Netherlands at 7 points in Group C; Tunisia and Saudi Arabia at 1 point in Group H. Both of these ties were resolved on total goal difference. Also, in both cases the teams had tied their match, so the order of ranking criteria made no difference.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finals_tournament">Finals tournament</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg/250px-FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg/375px-FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg/500px-FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FIFA_World_Cup_2006_Opening_Ceremony.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2006 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony in Munich</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The finals tournament of the 2006 World Cup began on 9 June. The 32 teams were divided into eight groups of four teams each, within which the teams competed in a round-robin tournament to determine which two of those four teams would advance to the sixteen-team knock-out stage, which started on 24 June. In total, 64 games were played.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hosting">Hosting</span></h3>
<p>Although Germany failed to win the Cup, the tournament was considered a great success for Germany in general. Germany also experienced a sudden increase in patriotic spirit with flag waving, traditionally frowned upon by German society since World War II, whenever the German team played.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> For the closing ceremonies, <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Keller_(musician)" title="Matthias Keller (musician)">Matthias Keller</a> composed a work performed simultaneously by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munich_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Munich Philharmonic Orchestra">Munich Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_State_Orchestra" title="Bavarian State Orchestra">Bavarian State Orchestra</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bavarian_Radio_Orchestra" title="Bavarian Radio Orchestra">Bavarian Radio Orchestra</a> with conductors <a href="/wiki/Christian_Thielemann" title="Christian Thielemann">Christian Thielemann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zubin_Mehta" title="Zubin Mehta">Zubin Mehta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mariss_Jansons" title="Mariss Jansons">Mariss Jansons</a>, and soloists <a href="/wiki/Diana_Damrau" title="Diana Damrau">Diana Damrau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Plácido Domingo">Plácido Domingo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lang_Lang_(pianist)" title="Lang Lang (pianist)">Lang Lang</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_powers_dominate">Traditional powers dominate</span></h3>
<p>Despite early success by <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana</a>, the tournament marked a return to dominance of the traditional football powers. Four years after a <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 tournament</a> in which teams from North America (<a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a>), Africa (<a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal</a>), and Asia (<a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea</a>) made it deep into the knockout stages and <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> finished third, all eight seeded teams progressed to the knockout stages, and none of the quarter-finalists were from outside Europe or South America. Six former champions took part in the quarter-final round, with Ukraine and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="2004 UEFA European Football Championship">Euro 2004</a> runners-up Portugal as the only relative outsiders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Argentina and Brazil were eliminated in the quarter-finals, leaving an all-European final four for only the fourth time (after the <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966</a> and <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a> tournaments).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scoring">Scoring</span></h3>
<p>Despite the early goals that flooded the group stages, the knock-out phase had a much lower goals per match ratio. A prime example of the dearth of goals was Portugal, which only scored in the 23rd minute of the Round of 16, and did not score again until the 88th minute of the third place play-off. No player managed to score a hat-trick in this tournament. Italy, Germany, Argentina, Brazil and France were the only teams to score more than one goal in a knockout match. Germany was one of the exceptions, tending to play an attacking style of football throughout the knock-out stage, which was reflected by the fact that they scored the most number of goals (14), with players from all three outfield positions (defence, midfield and forward) making the scoresheet.</p>
<p>Germany's <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Klose" title="Miroslav Klose">Miroslav Klose</a> scored five goals to claim the Golden Boot, the lowest total to win the prize since <a href="/wiki/1962_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1962 FIFA World Cup">1962</a>. No other player scored more than three goals. No player from the winning Italian squad scored more than two goals, though ten different players had scored for the team, tying France's record in <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a> for the most goalscorers from any one team.</p>
<p>For the first time ever in the FIFA World Cup, the first and last goals of the tournament were scored by defenders. <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Lahm" title="Philipp Lahm">Philipp Lahm</a>, the German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defender_(football)#Wingback" title="Defender (football)">left wingback</a>, scored the opener against Costa Rica after only 5 minutes of the opening match. In the final, <a href="/wiki/Marco_Materazzi" title="Marco Materazzi">Marco Materazzi</a>, the Italian centre back, out-jumped <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Vieira" title="Patrick Vieira">Patrick Vieira</a> and headed in the last goal of the 2006 FIFA World Cup.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unprecedented_number_of_cards">Unprecedented number of cards</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_disciplinary_record" title="2006 FIFA World Cup disciplinary record">2006 FIFA World Cup disciplinary record</a></div>
<p>The tournament had a record number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yellow_card_(sport)" title="Yellow card (sport)">yellow</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_card_(sports)" title="Red card (sports)">red cards</a>, breaking the previous record set by the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup#Tournament" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 World Cup</a>. Players received a record-breaking 345 yellow cards and 28 red cards, with Russian referee <a href="/wiki/Valentin_Valentinovich_Ivanov" title="Valentin Valentinovich Ivanov">Valentin Ivanov</a> handing out 16 yellow and 4 red cards in the round of 16 match between <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a>, in a match known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(2006_FIFA_World_Cup)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (2006 FIFA World Cup)">Battle of Nuremberg</a>. Portugal had two players suspended for each of the quarter-final and semi-final matches, respectively. FIFA President <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Blatter" title="Sepp Blatter">Sepp Blatter</a> hinted that he may allow some rule changes for future tournaments so that earlier accumulated bookings will not force players to miss the final, should their teams make it that far. The tournament also saw English referee <a href="/wiki/Graham_Poll" title="Graham Poll">Graham Poll</a> mistakenly hand out three yellow cards to Croatia's <a href="/wiki/Josip_%C5%A0imuni%C4%87" title="Josip Šimunić">Josip Šimunić</a> in their match against Australia.</p>
<p>The high number of yellow and red cards shown also prompted discussion about <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_officials" title="2006 FIFA World Cup officials">the referees</a>. FIFA Officials and President <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Blatter" title="Sepp Blatter">Sepp Blatter</a> received criticism for allegedly making rules too rigid and taking discretion away from referees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>

<li><b>GA</b> = total goals conceded (goals against)</li>
<li><b>GD</b> = goal difference (GF−GA)</li>
<li><b>Pts</b> = total points accumulated</li>
</ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_A">Group A</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_A" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group A">2006 FIFA World Cup Group A</a></div>
<p>In the opening match of the tournament, <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a> played a game which ended 4–2 for the host in the highest scoring opening match in the tournament's history. Germany went on to win the Group A after edging <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> and breezing past <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a> 3–0. Despite the defeat, Ecuador had already joined the host in the Round of 16 having beaten Poland and Costa Rica 2–0 and 3–0, respectively.</p>

<p><br/></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_B">Group B</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_B" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group B">2006 FIFA World Cup Group B</a></div>
<p>In Group B, <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> pushed <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a> into third place after narrow victories over the South Americans. <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">Trinidad and Tobago</a> earned some international respect after a draw with Sweden in their opening game and managing to hold England scoreless for 83 minutes, until goals from <a href="/wiki/Peter_Crouch" title="Peter Crouch">Peter Crouch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> sealed a 2–0 win for the Three Lions. Sweden qualified for the knockout rounds after drawing 2–2 with England to maintain their 38-year unbeaten record against them.</p>

<p><br/></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_C">Group C</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_C" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group C">2006 FIFA World Cup Group C</a></div>
<p>Both <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> qualified from Group C with a game remaining, Argentina topping the group on goal difference having hammered <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Serbia and Montenegro national football team">Serbia and Montenegro</a> 6–0 and beating <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_football_team" title="Ivory Coast national football team">Ivory Coast</a> 2–1. The Dutch picked up 1–0 and 2–1 victories over Serbia and Montenegro and Ivory Coast, respectively. Ivory Coast defeated Serbia and Montenegro 3–2 in their final game, in Serbia &amp; Montenegro's last ever international before the break-up of the country.</p>

<p><br/></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_D">Group D</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_D" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group D">2006 FIFA World Cup Group D</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> coasted through in Group D, picking up the maximum number of points, with <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> qualifying in second. <a href="/wiki/Iran_national_football_team" title="Iran national football team">Iran</a> missed chances against Mexico in their opening 1–3 defeat and were eliminated in their match against Portugal. They fought hard against the Portuguese, but went down 2–0. Their last game against <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_football_team" title="Angola national football team">Angola</a> ended in 1–1 draw. The Africans had a respectable first World Cup tournament after earning draws with Mexico (0–0) and Iran.</p>
<p><br/></p>

<p><br/></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_E">Group E</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_E" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group E">2006 FIFA World Cup Group E</a></div>
<p>In Group E, <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> went through to the Round of 16 conceding just one goal (an <a href="/wiki/Own_goal" title="Own goal">own goal</a>) in the group phase against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a>. The US bowed out of the tournament after disappointing results against the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team" title="Czech Republic national football team">Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghana_national_football_team" title="Ghana national football team">Ghana</a>, 0–3 and 1–2, respectively, despite a 1–1 draw (finishing with 9 vs 10 men) against Italy. Tournament debutant Ghana joined Italy in the round of 16, following victories over the Czech Republic and the United States. <a href="/wiki/Daniele_De_Rossi" title="Daniele De Rossi">Daniele De Rossi</a> was suspended for 4 games following his sending-off against the United States.</p>

<p><br/></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_F">Group F</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_F" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group F">2006 FIFA World Cup Group F</a></div>
<p>Group F included the reigning <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">World Champions</a> <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>. Playing in their first World Cup for 32 years, Australia came from behind to defeat Japan 3–1, and, despite losing 0–2 to Brazil, a 2–2 draw with Croatia was enough to give the Australians a place in the Round of 16 in a game where two players were sent-off for second bookings and one, erroneously, for a <a href="/wiki/List_of_2006_FIFA_World_Cup_controversies#Three_yellow_cards_issued_.28Croatia_vs._Australia.2C_group_stage.29" title="List of 2006 FIFA World Cup controversies">third booking</a> by English referee <a href="/wiki/Graham_Poll" title="Graham Poll">Graham Poll</a>. The Brazilians won all three games to qualify first in the group. Their 1–0 win against Croatia was through a goal late in the first-half by <a href="/wiki/Kak%C3%A1" title="Kaká">Kaká</a>. Croatia and Japan went out of the tournament without a single win.</p>
<p><br/></p>

<p><br/></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_G">Group G</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_G" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group G">2006 FIFA World Cup Group G</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> only managed a scoreless draw against <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> and a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea</a>. With captain <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a> suspended, their 2–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Togo_national_football_team" title="Togo national football team">Togo</a> was enough for them to advance to the knockout round. They were joined by the group winners, Switzerland, who defeated South Korea 2–0, and did not concede a goal in the tournament. South Korea won their first World Cup finals match outside their own country in defeating Togo, but four points were not enough to see them through to the round of 16 (the only team for which this was the case), while Togo exited without a point.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_H">Group H</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_H" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Group H">2006 FIFA World Cup Group H</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> dominated Group H, picking up the maximum number of points, scoring 8 goals, and conceding only 1. <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a>, despite being beaten 4–0 by Spain in their first World Cup game, took advantage of the weaker opponents to beat <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_national_football_team" title="Saudi Arabia national football team">Saudi Arabia</a> 4–0 and scrape past <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a> 1–0 thanks to a 70th-minute penalty by <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Shevchenko" title="Andriy Shevchenko">Andriy Shevchenko</a>, to reach the Round of 16. Saudi Arabia and Tunisia went out of the tournament having 1 point each, thanks to a 2–2 draw against each other.</p>

<p><br/></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Knockout_stage">Knockout stage</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage" title="2006 FIFA World Cup knockout stage">2006 FIFA World Cup knockout stage</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knockout stage</a> involved the sixteen teams that qualified from the group stage of the tournament. There were four rounds of matches, with each round eliminating half of the teams entering that round. The successive rounds were: round of 16, quarter-finals, semi-finals, and final. There was also a play-off to decide third/fourth place. For each game in the knockout stage, a draw was followed by thirty minutes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overtime_(association_football)" title="Overtime (association football)">extra time</a> (two 15-minute halves); if scores were still level there would be a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> (at least five penalties each, and more if necessary) to determine who progressed to the next round. Scores after extra time are indicated by (aet), and penalty shoot-outs are indicated by (pen.).</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Round_of_16">Round of 16</span></h4>
<p>In the second round, conceding two early goals in the first twelve minutes to Germany effectively ended the Swedes' hopes of progressing to the quarter-finals. Argentina struggled to get past Mexico until a <a href="/wiki/Maxi_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Maxi Rodríguez">Maxi Rodríguez</a> goal in extra time put the <i>Albiceleste</i> in the quarter-finals. Australia's journey ended when Italians were awarded a controversial penalty, scored by <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Totti" title="Francesco Totti">Francesco Totti</a>, deep into the remaining seconds of the match. The Italians had spent much of the game with only ten men on the field, following an equally controversial red card shown to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre-back" title="Centre-back">centre back</a> <a href="/wiki/Marco_Materazzi" title="Marco Materazzi">Marco Materazzi</a>. In a 0–0 match, Switzerland failed to convert any of their three penalties in the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> against Ukraine to see them exit the competition with an unwanted new record in becoming the first team in a World Cup to fail to convert any penalties in a shootout. Their elimination also meant that they became the first nation to be eliminated from the World Cup without conceding any goals (and indeed the only nation ever to participate in a World Cup finals tournament without conceding a goal).</p>
<p>England struggled against Ecuador but won 1–0 thanks to a <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> free kick. Brazil won 3–0 against Ghana, in a game which included <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>'s record 15th World Cup goal. <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> reported that the match may have been influenced by an Asian betting syndicate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Portugal defeated the Netherlands 1–0. The only goal came courtesy of a <a href="/wiki/Maniche" title="Maniche">Maniche</a> strike in an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(association_football)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (association football)">acrimonious match</a>, which marked a new World Cup record with 16 yellow cards (Portugal: 9, the Netherlands: 7) and 4 players being sent off for a second bookable offence. France came from behind to defeat Spain 3–1 thanks to goals from <a href="/wiki/Franck_Rib%C3%A9ry" title="Franck Ribéry">Franck Ribéry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Vieira" title="Patrick Vieira">Patrick Vieira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Quarter-finals">Quarter-finals</span></h4>
<p>Germany and Argentina ended 1–1 after extra time; the hosts edged out the Argentinians 4–2 on penalties to go through to the semifinals (this was the first time Argentina had lost a World Cup penalty shootout: up until this match, both Argentina and Germany had participated in three penalty shootouts, winning all of them). In <a href="/wiki/Veltins-Arena" title="Veltins-Arena">Gelsenkirchen</a>, when England faced Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> was sent off, and Portugal won the penalty shoot-out 3–1 after a 0–0 draw to reach their first World Cup semi-final since the days of <a href="/wiki/Eus%C3%A9bio" title="Eusébio">Eusébio</a> 40 years earlier, and ensure manager <a href="/wiki/Luiz_Felipe_Scolari" title="Luiz Felipe Scolari">Luiz Felipe Scolari</a>'s third consecutive tournament quarter-final win over <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-Göran Eriksson">Sven-Göran Eriksson</a>'s England.</p>
<p>Italy defeated quarter-final debutants Ukraine 3–0. France eliminated Brazil 1–0 to advance into the semi-finals. Brazil only managed one shot on goal, while <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>'s dribbling earned him Man of the Match and his free-kick to <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a> resulted in the winning goal.</p>
<div class="vevent" style="width: 100%; background-color: transparent; clear:both">

Attendance: 48,000<br/>
Referee: <a href="/wiki/Luis_Medina_Cantalejo" title="Luis Medina Cantalejo">Luis Medina Cantalejo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Football_Federation" title="Royal Spanish Football Federation">Spain</a>)</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-finals">Semi-finals</span></h4>
<p>With Argentina and Brazil eliminated in the quarter-finals, an all-European semi-final line up was completed for only the fourth time (after the <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934</a>, <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966</a> and <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a> tournaments).</p>
<p>The semi-final between Germany and Italy produced an extra time period that went scoreless until the 118th minute, when Italy scored twice through <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Grosso" title="Fabio Grosso">Fabio Grosso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Del_Piero" title="Alessandro Del Piero">Alessandro Del Piero</a>, putting an end to Germany's undefeated record in Dortmund. With this win, Italy continued their dominance over Germany.</p>
<p>In the second semi-final, Portugal lost to France 1–0 in <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Munich</a>. In a repeat of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1984" title="UEFA Euro 1984">Euro 1984</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a> semi-finals, Portugal were defeated by France, with the decisive goal being a penalty scored by France captain Zinedine Zidane.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_place_play-off">Third place play-off</span></h4>
<p>The hosts got three goals in 20 minutes in the second half with the help of 21-year-old left <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> <a href="/wiki/Bastian_Schweinsteiger" title="Bastian Schweinsteiger">Bastian Schweinsteiger</a>. His first goal beat the Portuguese goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_(footballer,_born_1976)" title="Ricardo (footballer, born 1976)">Ricardo</a> with pace over his head. Only 4 minutes later, Schweinsteiger's free kick 30 metres from the left of the penalty box, driven low across goal, was connected with <a href="/wiki/Petit_(Portuguese_footballer)" title="Petit (Portuguese footballer)">Petit</a>'s knee to become an own goal for Portugal. The German did not stop, and netted his second goal, which swerved away to the keeper's left, in the 78th minute.</p>
<p>Portugal were strong in possession but lacked punch in attack; unable to convert 57% possession into goals. <a href="/wiki/Pauleta" title="Pauleta">Pauleta</a> had two clear chances from 15 metres, but both times hit tame shots that did not trouble keeper <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Kahn" title="Oliver Kahn">Oliver Kahn</a>, who was playing in his last match for the German national team. Portugal got a consolation goal with the help of substitute <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="Luís Figo">Luís Figo</a> (also playing the final international game of his career), who almost immediately provided the precise distribution needed to unlock the German defence. A cross from the right wing on 88 minutes found fellow substitute <a href="/wiki/Nuno_Gomes" title="Nuno Gomes">Nuno Gomes</a> at the far post, who dived in for the goal. The game ended 3–1, a result which gave the tournament hosts the bronze medals and left Portugal in fourth place.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Final">Final</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Final">2006 FIFA World Cup Final</a></div>
<p>The final started with each side scoring within the first 20 minutes. Zinedine Zidane opened the scoring by converting a controversial seventh-minute penalty kick,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> which glanced off the underside of the crossbar and into the goal... before bouncing back up, hitting the crossbar again and bounced out of the goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Marco Materazzi then levelled the scores in the 19th minute following an <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Pirlo" title="Andrea Pirlo">Andrea Pirlo</a> corner. Both teams had chances to score the winning goal in normal time: <a href="/wiki/Luca_Toni" title="Luca Toni">Luca Toni</a> hit the crossbar in the 35th minute for Italy (he later had a header disallowed for offside), while France were not awarded a possible second penalty in the 53rd minute when <a href="/wiki/Florent_Malouda" title="Florent Malouda">Florent Malouda</a> went down in the box after a tackle from <a href="/wiki/Gianluca_Zambrotta" title="Gianluca Zambrotta">Gianluca Zambrotta</a>.</p>
<p>At the end of the regulation 90 minutes, the score was still level at 1–1, and the match was forced into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overtime_(association_football)" title="Overtime (association football)">extra time</a>. Italian goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Gianluigi_Buffon" title="Gianluigi Buffon">Gianluigi Buffon</a> made a potentially game-saving save in extra time when he tipped a Zidane header over the crossbar. Further controversy ensued near the end of extra time, when <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_Final#Zidane_sending_off" title="2006 FIFA World Cup Final">Zidane head-butted Materazzi</a> in the chest in an off-the-ball incident and was sent off. Extra time produced no further goals and a penalty shootout followed, which Italy won 5–3. France's <a href="/wiki/David_Trezeguet" title="David Trezeguet">David Trezeguet</a>, the man who scored the <a href="/wiki/Golden_goal" title="Golden goal">golden goal</a> against Italy in Euro 2000, was the only player not to score his penalty; his spot kick hit the crossbar, landed on the goal line and went out. It was the first all-European final since Italy's triumph over West Germany in the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 World Cup</a>, and the second final, after <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1994 FIFA World Cup Final">1994</a>, to be decided on penalties. It was also Italy's first world title in 24 years, and their fourth overall, making them the second most successful World Cup team ever. The victory also helped Italy top the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> in February 2007 for the first time since November 1993.</p>
<div class="vevent" style="width: 100%; background-color: transparent; clear:both">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_statistics" title="2006 FIFA World Cup statistics">2006 FIFA World Cup statistics</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goalscorers">Goalscorers</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Klose" title="Miroslav Klose">Miroslav Klose</a> received the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_awards#Golden_Boot" title="FIFA World Cup awards">Golden Boot</a> for scoring five goals in the World Cup. In total, 147 goals were scored by 110 different players, with four of them credited as own goals.</p>

<dt>5 goals</dt>
</dl>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assists">Assists</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Juan_Rom%C3%A1n_Riquelme" title="Juan Román Riquelme">Juan Román Riquelme</a> won the assists table with four assists.</p>
<dl>
<dt>4 assists</dt>
</dl>

<p>FIFA's Technical Study Group (TSG) also granted a <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" title="Man of the match">Man of the Match</a> award to one player in each match. Italy's <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Pirlo" title="Andrea Pirlo">Andrea Pirlo</a> won the most Man of the Match awards, with three in total. <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Klose" title="Miroslav Klose">Miroslav Klose</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agustin_Delgado" title="Agustin Delgado">Agustin Delgado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%A9_Roberto" title="Zé Roberto">Zé Roberto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Frei" title="Alexander Frei">Alexander Frei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ballack" title="Michael Ballack">Michael Ballack</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Vieira" title="Patrick Vieira">Patrick Vieira</a> each received two awards.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="All-star_team">All-star team</span></h3>
<p>The All-star team is a squad consisting of the 23 most impressive players at the 2006 World Cup, as selected by FIFA's Technical Study Group. The team was chosen from a shortlist of over 50 players, and was selected based on performances from the second round onwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_money">Prize money</span></h3>
<p>A total of <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">CHF332 million</a> was awarded to the 32 teams participating in the tournament. Each team who entered the competition received CHF2 million, with the biggest prize being CHF24.5 million, awarded to the winner of the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prize_money_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-prize_money-48">[48]</a></sup> Below is a complete list of the prize money allocated:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prize_money_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-prize_money-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>CHF7 million – To each team eliminated in the <a href="#Group_stage">group stage</a> (16 teams)</li>
<li>CHF8.5 million – To each team eliminated in the <a href="#Round_of_16">round of 16</a> (8 teams)</li>
<li>CHF11.5 million – To each team eliminated in the <a href="#Quarter-finals">quarter-finals</a> (4 teams)</li>
<li>CHF21.5 million – <a href="#Third_place_play-off">Fourth placed team</a> and <a href="#Third_place_play-off">Third placed team</a></li>
<li>CHF22.5 million – <a href="#Final">Runners-up</a></li>
<li>CHF24.5 million – <a href="#Final">Winner</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_standings">Final standings</span></h3>
<p>All 32 teams are ranked based on criteria which have been used by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Please note that a penalty shoot-out counts as a draw for both teams.</p>

Ein Sommermärchen</a></i>, a 2006 documentary film recording <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany national football team</a> from boot camp in Sardegna to third place playoff against <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Voices_from_the_FIFA_World_Cup" title="Voices from the FIFA World Cup">Voices from the FIFA World Cup</a></li>
<li>Several countries celebrated this major event with the minting of specially high value commemorative coins. Among them is the Belgian 20 euro <a href="/wiki/Euro_gold_and_silver_commemorative_coins_(Belgium)#2005_coinage" title="Euro gold and silver commemorative coins (Belgium)">Germany 2006 FIFA World Cup Coin</a>. The obverse of the coin shows a footballer with a ball, right above them '2006 FIFA World Cup Germany' can be clearly seen.</li>
